# Higham Chapter 20 Source Coverage Ledger

## Source and Scope

- Edition: Higham, *Accuracy and Stability of Numerical Algorithms*, 2nd ed. (SIAM, 2002), verified from repository metadata and the SIAM chapter PDF title metadata.
- Chapter: 20, "The Least Squares Problem".
- Source file: `References/1.9780898718027.ch20.pdf`.
- Printed pages: 381-406.
- Mode: core.
- Parallel split: 4.
- Planning documents consulted: `chapter_splitting/HIGHAM_PARALLEL_FORMALIZATION_BLUEPRINT.md`, Split 4 section of `chapter_splitting/split_primary_contracts.md`, and `chapter_splitting/chapter_index.md`.

- Latest addition: `rectSelfAdjointDilation_finiteOpNorm2Le_of_lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_zero`, `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_zero_finiteOpNorm2Le_iff_rectSelfAdjointDilation`, and `lsScaledAugmentedMatrix_zero_finiteOpNorm2Le_of_frobNormRect_le` complete the finite operator-2 bound equivalence between the source-indexed zero-scaled augmented matrix `C(0)` from (20.17) and the repository self-adjoint dilation, and add a conservative Frobenius-bound corollary for `C(0)`.  This gives the later (20.18)-(20.19) route a bidirectional operator-bound bridge at the `Fin (m+n)` source surface; it still does not prove the eigenvalue multiplicities, a spectral decomposition, a sharp operator norm, or the (20.19) matrix condition-number formula.

This gives the later (20.18)-(20.19) route an operator-bound bridge at the `Fin (m+n)` source surface; it does not prove the eigenvalue multiplicities, a spectral decomposition, an operator-norm equality, or the (20.19) matrix condition-number formula.

This transfers the repository's self-adjoint-dilation quadratic-form infrastructure to the source `Fin (m+n)` indexing used by (20.18)-(20.19); it does not prove the eigenvalue multiplicities, a spectral decomposition, an operator-norm equality, or the (20.19) matrix condition-number formula.

This connects the source action model to existing dilation vector-action infrastructure for later spectral/operator-norm work; it does not prove the (20.18) eigenvalue multiplicities, a spectral decomposition, or the (20.19) matrix condition-number formula.

This connects the source matrix to existing dilation infrastructure for later spectral/operator-norm work; it does not prove the (20.18) eigenvalue multiplicities, a spectral decomposition, or the (20.19) matrix condition-number formula.

This is a matrix-side prerequisite for the later (20.18)-(20.19) spectral/condition-number bridge; it does not prove the global eigenvalue multiplicities, a spectral decomposition, or the matrix condition-number formula.

Consequently, exact LS minimizers now close both residual branches: `eta_F(y)` and the printed `min {phi, sigma_min}` RHS are both zero and hence equal.  This still does not prove the general Walden--Karlson--Sun lower/attainment argument for non-minimizers, derive the eigenvalue branch formula, or handle the `theta = infinity` limiting case.
- Previous addition: `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_left_residual_col_sum_eq_zero`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_right_residual_col_sum_eq_zero`, `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_residual_leftNull_of_column_orthogonal`, and `lsNormwiseBackwardErrorFormulaMatrix_residual_leftNull_of_isLeastSquaresMinimizer` add the nonzero-residual left-null certificate for the WKS source block in (20.21). - Previous addition: `lsScaledAugmentedBranchRatio_gt_sigma_ratio_sq_of_alpha_eq_sigmaMax` adds a source-facing scalar witness for the `max_alpha kappa_2(C(alpha)) > kappa_2(A)^2` side of (20.19). For positive extremal singular values and scaling `alpha = sigmaMax`, the extremal branch ratio is strictly larger than `(sigmaMax / sigmaMin)^2`. This is still scalar branch algebra; it does not prove the global spectral multiplicities in (20.18) or connect the branch ratio to the matrix condition number of `C(alpha)`.
- Previous addition: `lseWeightedMinimizer_constraintResidual_normSq_tendsto_zero_of_inv_mu_sq` and `lseWeightedMinimizer_constraintResidual_norm_tendsto_zero_of_inv_mu_sq` add a sequence-level feasibility-convergence step for the method of weighting in (20.26). Under exact weighted minimizers, a feasible constrained comparator, nonzero weights, and `(mu^2)^{-1} -> 0`, the equality-constraint residual tends to zero in squared norm and norm. This still does not prove convergence of the weighted minimizers to the unique LSE solution, existence or continuity of a selected minimizer branch, or weighted-method stability.

They prove the weighted objective dominates the equality-constraint penalty and that an exact weighted minimizer has squared constraint residual bounded by any feasible constrained objective divided by `mu^2`. This supports the source approximation discussion but still does not prove the full limiting theorem as `mu -> infinity` or any weighted-method stability claim.

- Latest addition: `lseEliminationBlockMatrix`, `lseEliminationBlockMatrix_mulVec`, `lseEliminationBackSubstitution`, `lseEliminationBlockConstraint_eq_qtd_of_left_inverse`, `lseEliminationReducedAction`, `lseEliminationReducedRhs`, `lseEliminationResidual_eq_reduced`, `lseEliminationReducedObjective`, `lseEliminationObjective_eq_reduced`, `IsLSEEliminationReducedMinimizer`, `lseEliminationBackSubstitution_eq_of_block_constraint`, `lseElimination_isLSEMinimizer_of_reduced_minimizer`, `IsLSEMinimizer.of_permuteCols`, and `lseElimination_isLSEMinimizer_original_of_reduced_minimizer` formalize the exact post-pivot elimination algebra in (20.29)-(20.30): with supplied two-sided `R1^{-1}` action and `qtd = Q^T d`, back-substitution satisfies the transformed constraint, feasible partitioned vectors have the same back-substitution form, the full `[A1 A2]` residual/objective reduces to the Schur-complement action `(A2 - A1 R1^{-1} R2)x2` and right-hand side `b - A1 R1^{-1}qtd`, a reduced minimizer lifts to an exact block-coordinate LSE minimizer, and the result pulls back through the column permutation `Π` to the original variables. QR with column pivoting and construction of the inverse action remain open.
- Latest addition: `lsAugmentedInverseActionTop`, `lsAugmentedInverseActionBottom`, `LSAugmentedSystem.of_eq20_6_inverse_action`, `rectLSGram_symmetric`, `lsGramNonsingInv`, `lsAplusOfGramNonsingInv`, `lsGramNonsingInv_isInverse_of_det_ne_zero`, `lsGramNonsingInv_symmetric`, and `LSAugmentedSystem.of_eq20_6_nonsing_gram` formalize the exact inverse-block action in (20.6), first under supplied inverse data and then with the concrete repository inverse candidate under `det(A^T A) != 0`.

Additional (20.26) increment: `lseWeightedConstraintPenalty_le_objective`, `lseConstraintResidual_normSq_le_of_weightedObjective_le`, `lseConstraintResidual_norm_le_sqrt_div_of_weightedObjective_le`, and `lseWeightedMinimizer_constraintResidual_normSq_le_feasibleObjective_div_mu_sq` were added as finite-weight coercivity support for the method of weighting.  They prove that the weighted objective dominates `mu^2 * ||Bx-d||_2^2`, that any candidate with weighted objective at most `R` has constraint residual bounded by `R / mu^2` in squared norm, and that an exact minimizer of the weighted problem inherits such a bound from any feasible constrained comparator.  This does not prove convergence as `mu -> infinity`, existence/continuity of a selected minimizer branch, or any finite-precision weighted-method stability theorem. Current exact-residual WKS branches: the source-residual hypothesis `lsResidualHigham A b y = 0` directly gives an exact least-squares minimizer, zero printed RHS, and `eta_F =` the printed (20.21) RHS.  For an exact minimizer with nonzero source residual, the residual annihilates the source block from the left, which now forces row-rank deficiency, `sigma_min = 0`, zero printed RHS, and `eta_F =` the printed RHS.  The remaining general WKS work is the nonzero-residual spectral lower-bound/attainment argument for non-minimizers and the eigenvalue/limiting-case material.

## Next Row

The next highest-leverage implementation-facing row remains Theorem 20.3: discharge or replace the stronger no-pivot diagonal-dominance/finite-max side conditions in the new source-facing stored-Householder theorem, or connect them to a source-equivalent QR construction with pivoting/nonbreakdown data. For Section 20.5, the finite max-component, recursive growth-coefficient package, closed-growth package, gamma-only closed-growth package, single-gamma-index package, and factorized printed-radius package now exist; the next implementation-facing step is to remove the remaining extra factor `2 * householderQRRhsPanelGammaClosedGrowthFactor (n+k) n`, or justify it under explicit source-visible assumptions, to reach Higham's printed `sqrt(n+k) * n * gamma` RHS coefficient. The next spectral step for the scaled augmented matrix is Problem 20.7's full (20.18) spectral multiplicity theorem and the matrix condition-number bridge for (20.19); the `C(alpha)` symmetry bridge, `C(0)` self-adjoint-dilation matrix/action/Rayleigh/operator-bound bridges, scalar balanced-scaling, and `alpha = sigmaMax` branch-ratio certificates are now covered. For the normwise backward-error row, the next step is the actual Walden--Karlson--Sun spectral certificate for the alternative formula (20.21): prove the lower bound against every feasible perturbation and construct an attaining feasible perturbation for the printed `min {phi, sigma_min [A phi(I-r r^+)]}` RHS, then prove the eigenvalue branch formula and any selected `theta = infinity` limiting case. The next LSE row is Theorem 20.9's GQR existence proof plus proof of the top-zero/lower-triangular reconstruction hypotheses from the QR construction/actual factors.
